     1	//! `RunSync` — manual reconciliation action.
     2	//!
     3	//! Implements [`ActionModule`] so apps can wire a "sync now" button to the
     4	//! M4 engine without inventing per-relay surface area.  The action accepts a
     5	//! list of `(filter_hash, relay_url)` targets, runs them through the
     6	//! reconciler, and emits a [`RunSyncOutput`] summary.
     7	//!
     8	//! The reduce step here is *thin* — the real work happens at the planner /
     9	//! actor layer where the bytes actually fly across the wire.  This module is
    10	//! the orchestration shell; it lets the action surface a `busy` flag and a
    11	//! `toast` field per D6 without hand-rolling action plumbing in every app.
    12	
    13	use nmp_core::substrate::{
    14	    ActionContext, ActionId, ActionInput, ActionModule, ActionPlan, ActionRejection,
    15	    ActionStatus, ActionTransition,
    16	};
    17	use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
    18	
    19	/// Action namespace; surfaced as the public `NAMESPACE` constant on
    20	/// [`RunSync`] for the codegen tool.
    21	pub const ACTION_NAMESPACE: &str = "nmp.nip77.run_sync";
    22	
    23	/// What the user requests when invoking `RunSync`.
    24	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Deserialize, Serialize)]
    25	pub struct RunSyncAction {
    26	    /// `(filter_hash_hex, relay_url)` targets.  Empty list ⇒ reconcile every
    27	    /// open pair the trigger engine knows about (the actor expands this).
    28	    pub targets: Vec<(String, String)>,
    29	    /// Optional deadline in milliseconds since epoch.
    30	    pub deadline_ms: Option<u64>,
    31	}
    32	
    33	/// Steps the action transitions through.  Stored as a small enum so a
    34	/// crashing app can resume from disk without losing more than one step.
    35	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Deserialize, PartialEq, Serialize)]
    36	pub enum RunSyncStep {
    37	    Prepared { remaining: u32 },
    38	    Running { remaining: u32, completed: u32 },
    39	    Finalising,
    40	}
    41	
    42	/// Final summary the action emits on success.
    43	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Deserialize, PartialEq, Serialize)]
    44	pub struct RunSyncOutput {
    45	    pub completed: u32,
    46	    pub bytes_on_wire_via_neg: u64,
    47	    pub bytes_saved_vs_req: u64,
    48	}
    49	
    50	/// `ActionModule` implementation.
    51	pub struct RunSync;
    52	
    53	impl ActionModule for RunSync {
    54	    const NAMESPACE: &'static str = ACTION_NAMESPACE;
    55	
    56	    type Action = RunSyncAction;
    57	    type Step = RunSyncStep;
    58	    type Output = RunSyncOutput;
    59	
    60	    fn start(
    61	        _ctx: &mut ActionContext,
    62	        action: Self::Action,
    63	    ) -> Result<ActionPlan<Self::Step>, ActionRejection> {
    64	        let target_count = action.targets.len() as u32;
    65	        Ok(ActionPlan {
    66	            initial_step: RunSyncStep::Prepared {
    67	                remaining: target_count,
    68	            },
    69	            initial_status: ActionStatus::Pending,
    70	            deadline_ms: action.deadline_ms,
    71	        })
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    fn reduce(
    75	        _ctx: &mut ActionContext,
    76	        _id: ActionId,
    77	        input: ActionInput<Self::Step>,
    78	    ) -> ActionTransition<Self::Step, Self::Output> {
    79	        match input {
    80	            ActionInput::Started => ActionTransition::Continue {
    81	                step: RunSyncStep::Running {
    82	                    remaining: 0,
    83	                    completed: 0,
    84	                },
    85	                status: ActionStatus::Running,
    86	            },
    87	            ActionInput::ResumedAfterRestart { step } => ActionTransition::Continue {
    88	                step,
    89	                status: ActionStatus::Running,
    90	            },
    91	            ActionInput::CapabilityResult { value } => match parse_progress(&value) {
    92	                Ok(progress) => {
    93	                    if progress.remaining == 0 {
    94	                        ActionTransition::Complete {
    95	                            output: RunSyncOutput {
    96	                                completed: progress.completed,
    97	                                bytes_on_wire_via_neg: progress
    98	                                    .bytes_on_wire_via_neg
    99	                                    .unwrap_or(0),
   100	                                bytes_saved_vs_req: progress.bytes_saved_vs_req.unwrap_or(0),
   101	                            },
   102	                        }
   103	                    } else {
   104	                        ActionTransition::Continue {
   105	                            step: RunSyncStep::Running {
   106	                                remaining: progress.remaining,
   107	                                completed: progress.completed,
   108	                            },
   109	                            status: ActionStatus::Running,
   110	                        }
   111	                    }
   112	                }
   113	                Err(err) => ActionTransition::Fail {
   114	                    reason: format!("malformed capability payload: {err}"),
   115	                    transient: false,
   116	                },
   117	            },
   118	            ActionInput::RelayOk { .. } => ActionTransition::Continue {
   119	                step: RunSyncStep::Running {
   120	                    remaining: 0,
   121	                    completed: 0,
   122	                },
   123	                status: ActionStatus::Running,
   124	            },
   125	            ActionInput::Timeout => ActionTransition::Fail {
   126	                reason: "deadline exceeded".into(),
   127	                transient: true,
   128	            },
   129	            ActionInput::Cancel => ActionTransition::Fail {
   130	                reason: "cancelled by user".into(),
   131	                transient: false,
   132	            },
   133	        }
   134	    }
   135	}
   136	
   137	#[derive(Deserialize)]
   138	struct ProgressPayload {
   139	    completed: u32,
   140	    remaining: u32,
   141	    bytes_on_wire_via_neg: Option<u64>,
   142	    bytes_saved_vs_req: Option<u64>,
   143	}
   144	
   145	fn parse_progress(value: &serde_json::Value) -> Result<ProgressPayload, String> {
   146	    serde_json::from_value(value.clone()).map_err(|e| e.to_string())
   147	}
   148	
   149	/// Helper for tests / actor: finalise a `Running` step into an output.
   150	pub fn finalise(
   151	    completed: u32,
   152	    bytes_on_wire_via_neg: u64,
   153	    bytes_saved_vs_req: u64,
   154	) -> ActionTransition<RunSyncStep, RunSyncOutput> {
   155	    ActionTransition::Complete {
     1	//! Trigger fan-out for the three sync triggers documented in
     2	//! `docs/plan/m4-negentropy.md`:
     3	//!
     4	//! 1. **app foreground** → reconcile every open `(filter, relay)` against its
     5	//!    persisted watermark.
     6	//! 2. **view open with gap** → reconcile the specific pair the freshly-opened
     7	//!    view depends on.
     8	//! 3. **relay reconnect** → reconcile every `(filter, _)` against the relay
     9	//!    that just came back.
    10	//!
    11	//! ## Design
    12	//!
    13	//! The [`TriggerEngine`] owns the open-filter map and, for each trigger
    14	//! event, produces a deduplicated work list ([`ReconcileWork`]).  The list
    15	//! goes to the planner / actor for execution; the engine itself never opens
    16	//! a socket or touches the store.  This keeps the trigger layer pure-data
    17	//! and unit-testable without a relay harness.
    18	//!
    19	//! ## Doctrine
    20	//!
    21	//! * **D2** — every trigger results in a sync request before any REQ is
    22	//!   considered.
    23	//! * **D6** — the trigger surface is `Result`-free: failures (e.g. unknown
    24	//!   filter hash) are silently dropped; observable consequences land as
    25	//!   metrics, not exceptions.
    26	//! * **D8** — the dedup pass keeps the work list bounded by the open-filter
    27	//!   count, not by trigger throughput.
    28	
    29	use std::collections::{BTreeMap, BTreeSet};
    30	
    31	/// A trigger event the engine knows how to handle.
    32	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    33	pub enum TriggerEvent {
    34	    /// App came back to the foreground.
    35	    Foreground,
    36	    /// A view was just opened with the given `(filter_hash, relay_url)`
    37	    /// dependency.  Use this *only* when the view's coverage check already
    38	    /// produced `PartialUpTo` / `Unknown`; views that hit `CompleteAsOf`
    39	    /// should never reach this trigger.
    40	    ViewOpenedWithGap {
    41	        filter_hash: [u8; 32],
    42	        relay_url: String,
    43	    },
    44	    /// A relay reconnected (e.g. network resumed, WebSocket reopened).
    45	    RelayReconnected { relay_url: String },
    46	}
    47	
    48	/// One unit of reconciliation work emitted by the engine.
    49	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, Ord, PartialEq, PartialOrd)]
    50	pub struct ReconcileWork {
    51	    pub filter_hash: [u8; 32],
    52	    pub relay_url: String,
    53	}
    54	
    55	/// In-memory book-keeping for the trigger engine.
    56	pub struct TriggerEngine {
    57	    /// `(relay_url, filter_hash)` pairs currently held open by views.  The
    58	    /// `BTreeMap`/`BTreeSet` choice gives the engine deterministic output
    59	    /// order — useful for tests and for diffing diagnostic snapshots.
    60	    open: BTreeMap<String, BTreeSet<[u8; 32]>>,
    61	}
    62	
    63	impl TriggerEngine {
    64	    pub fn new() -> Self {
    65	        Self {
    66	            open: BTreeMap::new(),
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	
    70	    /// Register an open `(filter, relay)` pair.  Calling [`register`] twice
    71	    /// for the same pair is a no-op (set semantics).
    72	    pub fn register(&mut self, filter_hash: [u8; 32], relay_url: impl Into<String>) {
    73	        self.open
    74	            .entry(relay_url.into())
    75	            .or_default()
    76	            .insert(filter_hash);
    77	    }
    78	
    79	    /// Drop a previously-registered pair.  Idempotent.
    80	    pub fn unregister(&mut self, filter_hash: &[u8; 32], relay_url: &str) {
    81	        if let Some(set) = self.open.get_mut(relay_url) {
    82	            set.remove(filter_hash);
    83	            if set.is_empty() {
    84	                self.open.remove(relay_url);
    85	            }
    86	        }
    87	    }
    88	
    89	    /// True iff at least one pair is registered.
    90	    pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool {
    91	        self.open.is_empty()
    92	    }
    93	
    94	    /// Map a trigger event to its reconciliation work list.  Output order is
    95	    /// deterministic (relay-url-major, filter-hash-minor).
    96	    pub fn on_event(&self, event: TriggerEvent) -> Vec<ReconcileWork> {
    97	        let mut out: BTreeSet<ReconcileWork> = BTreeSet::new();
    98	        match event {
    99	            TriggerEvent::Foreground => {
   100	                for (relay, filters) in &self.open {
   101	                    for fh in filters {
   102	                        out.insert(ReconcileWork {
   103	                            filter_hash: *fh,
   104	                            relay_url: relay.clone(),
   105	                        });
   106	                    }
   107	                }
   108	            }
   109	            TriggerEvent::ViewOpenedWithGap {
   110	                filter_hash,
   111	                relay_url,
   112	            } => {
   113	                out.insert(ReconcileWork {
   114	                    filter_hash,
   115	                    relay_url,
   116	                });
   117	            }
   118	            TriggerEvent::RelayReconnected { relay_url } => {
   119	                if let Some(filters) = self.open.get(&relay_url) {
   120	                    for fh in filters {
   121	                        out.insert(ReconcileWork {
   122	                            filter_hash: *fh,
   123	                            relay_url: relay_url.clone(),
   124	                        });
   125	                    }
   126	                }
   127	            }
   128	        }
   129	        out.into_iter().collect()
   130	    }
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl Default for TriggerEngine {
   134	    fn default() -> Self {
   135	        Self::new()

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	//! Per-relay NIP-77 capability negotiation.
     2	//!
     3	//! A relay either supports the `NEG-OPEN` verb or it doesn't.  We discover
     4	//! support by probing once on first connect; the result is cached so future
     5	//! reconciliations skip the probe.  The cache is owned by the M4 substrate;
     6	//! persistence is layered on top by [`crate::capability_domain::CapabilityDomain`].
     7	//!
     8	//! ## Probe state machine
     9	//!
    10	//! ```text
    11	//!  ┌──────────┐  start_probe        ┌───────────┐
    12	//!  │  Unknown │ ───────────────────▶│  Probing  │
    13	//!  └──────────┘                     └──────┬────┘
    14	//!                                          │
    15	//!                          ┌── NEG-MSG ────┤── NEG-ERR ──┐
    16	//!                          ▼                              ▼
    17	//!                  ┌──────────────┐               ┌──────────────┐
    18	//!                  │ Supported    │               │ Unsupported  │
    19	//!                  └──────────────┘               └──────────────┘
    20	//! ```
    21	//!
    22	//! `Supported` and `Unsupported` are terminal in normal operation.  A relay
    23	//! that downgrades or revokes support requires an explicit reset (e.g. a
    24	//! manual `RunSync` invocation) — same policy as `nostr-sdk`'s capability
    25	//! tracking.
    26	
    27	use std::collections::HashMap;
    28	use std::sync::Mutex;
    29	
    30	/// What we believe about a relay's NIP-77 support.
    31	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    32	pub struct RelayCapabilities {
    33	    pub supports_nip77: bool,
    34	}
    35	
    36	/// Probe lifecycle state for a single relay.
    37	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    38	pub enum ProbeState {
    39	    Unknown,
    40	    Probing,
    41	    Supported,
    42	    Unsupported,
    43	}
    44	
    45	/// What a probe transition produces — used by callers to drive next steps.
    46	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    47	pub enum ProbeOutcome {
    48	    /// Probe was already complete; no further work.
    49	    AlreadySettled(RelayCapabilities),
    50	    /// Probe transitioned to a terminal state on this call.
    51	    Settled(RelayCapabilities),
    52	    /// Probe is in flight; caller must wait for the next relay frame.
    53	    Pending,
    54	}
    55	
    56	/// In-memory cache of per-relay capabilities.
    57	///
    58	/// Implementations are free to back the cache with disk (see
    59	/// [`crate::capability_domain::CapabilityDomain`]) — the trait is the
    60	/// minimal substrate the M4 reconciler depends on.
    61	pub trait CapabilityCache: Send + Sync {
    62	    fn get(&self, relay_url: &str) -> Option<RelayCapabilities>;
    63	    fn set(&self, relay_url: &str, caps: RelayCapabilities);
    64	    fn state(&self, relay_url: &str) -> ProbeState;
    65	    fn set_state(&self, relay_url: &str, state: ProbeState);
    66	}
    67	
    68	/// Lock-protected `HashMap` implementation of [`CapabilityCache`].  Adequate
    69	/// for app-lifetime usage; persistence is layered on top by the domain
    70	/// module.
    71	pub struct InMemoryCapabilityCache {
    72	    inner: Mutex<Inner>,
    73	}
    74	
    75	#[derive(Default)]
    76	struct Inner {
    77	    caps: HashMap<String, RelayCapabilities>,
    78	    state: HashMap<String, ProbeState>,
    79	}
    80	
    81	impl InMemoryCapabilityCache {
    82	    pub fn new() -> Self {
    83	        Self {
    84	            inner: Mutex::new(Inner::default()),
    85	        }
    86	    }
    87	}
    88	
    89	impl Default for InMemoryCapabilityCache {
    90	    fn default() -> Self {
    91	        Self::new()
    92	    }
    93	}
    94	
    95	impl CapabilityCache for InMemoryCapabilityCache {
    96	    fn get(&self, relay_url: &str) -> Option<RelayCapabilities> {
    97	        self.inner
    98	            .lock()
    99	            .expect("capability cache lock poisoned")
   100	            .caps
   101	            .get(relay_url)
   102	            .copied()
   103	    }
   104	
   105	    fn set(&self, relay_url: &str, caps: RelayCapabilities) {
   106	        let mut guard = self.inner.lock().expect("capability cache lock poisoned");
   107	        guard.caps.insert(relay_url.to_string(), caps);
   108	        guard.state.insert(
   109	            relay_url.to_string(),
   110	            if caps.supports_nip77 {
   111	                ProbeState::Supported
   112	            } else {
   113	                ProbeState::Unsupported
   114	            },
   115	        );
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    fn state(&self, relay_url: &str) -> ProbeState {
   119	        self.inner
   120	            .lock()
   121	            .expect("capability cache lock poisoned")
   122	            .state
   123	            .get(relay_url)
   124	            .copied()
   125	            .unwrap_or(ProbeState::Unknown)
   126	    }
   127	
   128	    fn set_state(&self, relay_url: &str, state: ProbeState) {
   129	        self.inner
   130	            .lock()
   131	            .expect("capability cache lock poisoned")
   132	            .state
   133	            .insert(relay_url.to_string(), state);
   134	    }
   135	}
   136	
   137	/// Drives the probe state machine for one relay.
   138	pub struct CapabilityProbe<'a> {
   139	    relay_url: String,
   140	    cache: &'a dyn CapabilityCache,
   141	}
   142	
   143	impl<'a> CapabilityProbe<'a> {
   144	    pub fn new(relay_url: impl Into<String>, cache: &'a dyn CapabilityCache) -> Self {
   145	        Self {
   146	            relay_url: relay_url.into(),
   147	            cache,
   148	        }
   149	    }
   150	
   151	    /// Begin probing if not already settled.  Callers should issue a
   152	    /// `NEG-OPEN` frame after this call returns [`ProbeOutcome::Pending`].
   153	    pub fn begin(&self) -> ProbeOutcome {
   154	        match self.cache.state(&self.relay_url) {
   155	            ProbeState::Supported => ProbeOutcome::AlreadySettled(RelayCapabilities {
   156	                supports_nip77: true,
   157	            }),
   158	            ProbeState::Unsupported => ProbeOutcome::AlreadySettled(RelayCapabilities {
   159	                supports_nip77: false,
   160	            }),
   161	            ProbeState::Probing | ProbeState::Unknown => {
   162	                self.cache.set_state(&self.relay_url, ProbeState::Probing);
   163	                ProbeOutcome::Pending
   164	            }
   165	        }
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    /// Settle the probe given the relay's first response frame.  Pass
   169	    /// `Some(true)` for `supported` after observing a `NEG-MSG`, `Some(false)`
   170	    /// after a `NEG-ERR` with an "unsupported"/"command not recognised"-style
   171	    /// reason, or `None` to leave the probe pending (e.g. the frame was for a
   172	    /// different sub-id).
   173	    pub fn settle(&self, supported: Option<bool>) -> ProbeOutcome {
   174	        let Some(value) = supported else {
   175	            return ProbeOutcome::Pending;
   176	        };
   177	        let caps = RelayCapabilities {
   178	            supports_nip77: value,
   179	        };
   180	        self.cache.set(&self.relay_url, caps);
   181	        ProbeOutcome::Settled(caps)
   182	    }
   183	}
   184	
   185	#[cfg(test)]
     1	//! Persistent per-relay capability rows.
     2	//!
     3	//! Exposes [`CapabilityDomain`] as a [`DomainModule`] so the kernel store
     4	//! keeps an LMDB sub-database of `(relay_url, RelayCapabilities)` pairs
     5	//! across launches.  This is the durable backing for the in-memory
     6	//! [`crate::capability::InMemoryCapabilityCache`].
     7	//!
     8	//! ## Schema
     9	//!
    10	//! `CapabilityRow` is the on-disk record:
    11	//!
    12	//! ```json
    13	//! { "relay_url": "wss://r.example/", "supports_nip77": true, "updated_at_s": 1700000000 }
    14	//! ```
    15	//!
    16	//! Encoded as serde-JSON for human-readability in `nmp dump`; the schema is
    17	//! intentionally narrow — capability ground truth lives in this module only,
    18	//! per D4 (single writer per fact).
    19	
    20	use nmp_core::substrate::{
    21	    DomainIndex, DomainMigration, DomainModule, DomainRegistry,
    22	};
    23	use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
    24	
    25	use crate::capability::{CapabilityCache, RelayCapabilities};
    26	
    27	/// The on-disk record persisted per relay URL.
    28	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Deserialize, Eq, PartialEq, Serialize)]
    29	pub struct CapabilityRow {
    30	    pub relay_url: String,
    31	    pub supports_nip77: bool,
    32	    pub updated_at_s: u64,
    33	}
    34	
    35	impl CapabilityRow {
    36	    pub fn capabilities(&self) -> RelayCapabilities {
    37	        RelayCapabilities {
    38	            supports_nip77: self.supports_nip77,
    39	        }
    40	    }
    41	}
    42	
    43	/// `DomainModule` that owns the capability sub-database.
    44	pub struct CapabilityDomain;
    45	
    46	impl DomainModule for CapabilityDomain {
    47	    const NAMESPACE: &'static str = "nmp.nip77.capabilities";
    48	    const SCHEMA_VERSION: u32 = 1;
    49	
    50	    fn migrations() -> Vec<DomainMigration> {
    51	        Vec::new()
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    fn indexes() -> Vec<DomainIndex> {
    55	        vec![DomainIndex {
    56	            name: "by_supports_nip77",
    57	            key_fn: |bytes| {
    58	                serde_json::from_slice::<CapabilityRow>(bytes)
    59	                    .ok()
    60	                    .map(|row| row.supports_nip77.to_string().into_bytes())
    61	            },
    62	        }]
    63	    }
    64	
    65	    fn register(registry: &mut DomainRegistry) {
    66	        registry.register_record::<CapabilityRow>();
    67	    }
    68	}
    69	
    70	/// Hydrate an in-memory cache from a previously-persisted set of rows.
    71	///
    72	/// Typical pre-startup flow: open the LMDB store, scan the capability
    73	/// sub-database, call [`hydrate_cache`] with the iterator.  The cache is
    74	/// then ready before any reconciliation runs.
    75	pub fn hydrate_cache<I>(cache: &dyn CapabilityCache, rows: I)
    76	where
    77	    I: IntoIterator<Item = CapabilityRow>,
    78	{
    79	    for row in rows {
    80	        cache.set(&row.relay_url, row.capabilities());
    81	    }
    82	}
    83	
    84	#[cfg(test)]
    85	mod tests {
    86	    use super::*;
    87	    use crate::capability::InMemoryCapabilityCache;
    88	
    89	    #[test]
    90	    fn schema_metadata_is_stable() {
    91	        assert_eq!(CapabilityDomain::NAMESPACE, "nmp.nip77.capabilities");
    92	        assert_eq!(CapabilityDomain::SCHEMA_VERSION, 1);
    93	        assert!(CapabilityDomain::migrations().is_empty());
    94	        assert_eq!(CapabilityDomain::indexes().len(), 1);
    95	    }

//! LMDB `EventStore` backend — skeleton for M3 phase 2.
//!
//! All methods return `StoreError::Io("lmdb-backend feature not enabled")` when
//! compiled without the `lmdb-backend` feature (which is the case in this M3
//! phase-1 deliverable). The full implementation is deferred to the follow-up
//! M3-lmdb task.
//!
//! See `docs/design/lmdb/trait.md` §5 and `docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md`.

use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};

use super::events::{DomainHandle, EventIter, EventStore};
use super::types::{
    ClaimerId, Coverage, DeleteFilter, DumpFormat, DumpStats, EventId, GcBudget, GcReport,
    InsertOutcome, ProvenanceEntry, PubKey, RelayUrl, StoredEvent, TombstoneRow,
    VerifiedEvent, WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow,
};
use super::StoreError;
use crate::substrate::DomainMigration;

/// Production LMDB-backed `EventStore`.
///
/// Architecture (ADR-0011): two separate heed environments.
/// - `path/nostr/` — owned by `nostr-lmdb` (upstream crate, eventual integration).
/// - `path/nmp/`   — owned by NMP; holds watermarks, domain rows, provenance, GC metadata.
///
/// Atomicity across the two environments is best-effort with startup repair.
pub struct LmdbEventStore {
    #[allow(dead_code)] // Used by lmdb-backend feature; skeleton in M3 phase 1.
    path: PathBuf,
    _private: (),
}

impl LmdbEventStore {
    /// Open or create an LMDB store at `path`.
    ///
    /// Creates `path/nostr/` and `path/nmp/` subdirectories.
    pub fn open(path: &Path) -> Result<Self, StoreError> {
        #[cfg(feature = "lmdb-backend")]
        {
            let nostr_dir = path.join("nostr");
            let nmp_dir = path.join("nmp");
            std::fs::create_dir_all(&nostr_dir)
                .map_err(|e| StoreError::Io(e.to_string()))?;
            std::fs::create_dir_all(&nmp_dir)
                .map_err(|e| StoreError::Io(e.to_string()))?;
            return Ok(Self { path: path.to_owned(), _private: () });
        }

        // Without lmdb-backend: store the path for future use, then fail.
        let _ = path;
        Err(StoreError::Io(
            "lmdb-backend feature not enabled — recompile with --features lmdb-backend".into(),
        ))
    }

    fn not_enabled() -> StoreError {
        StoreError::Io("lmdb-backend feature not enabled".into())
    }
}

impl EventStore for LmdbEventStore {
    fn get_by_id(&self, _id: &EventId) -> Result<Option<StoredEvent>, StoreError> {
        Err(Self::not_enabled())
    }

    fn scan_by_author_kind<'a>(
        &'a self,
        _author: &PubKey,
        _kinds: &[u32],
        _since: Option<u64>,
        _until: Option<u64>,
        _limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError> {
        Err(Self::not_enabled())
    }

    fn get_param_replaceable(
        &self,
        _pubkey: &PubKey,

    ) -> Result<Option<StoredEvent>, StoreError> {
        Err(Self::not_enabled())

        &'a self,
        _kind: u32,
        _d_tag: &[u8],
        _since: Option<u64>,
        _until: Option<u64>,
        _limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError> {
        Err(Self::not_enabled())
    }

    fn scan_by_etag<'a>(
        &'a self,
        _target: &EventId,
        _kinds: &[u32],
        _limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError> {
        Err(Self::not_enabled())
    }

        &'a self,
        _target: &PubKey,

    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError> {

    {

    }

# LMDB sub-design: `EventStore` trait

> Part of [`docs/design/lmdb-schema.md`](../lmdb-schema.md).
> Supporting types are in [`trait/types.md`](trait/types.md) (extracted to keep this file ≤ 300 LOC).

## 1. Crate placement

`crates/nmp-core/src/store/events.rs` (filename note: `trait` is a Rust keyword, so the file is named `events.rs` and exposes `pub trait EventStore`). Re-exported from `nmp_core::store::EventStore`. The actor (`crates/nmp-core/src/actor.rs`) holds the store as `store: Box<dyn EventStore>`; backends are constructed by the factory in `store/mod.rs::open_event_store(&AppConfig) -> Result<Box<dyn EventStore>, StoreError>`.

All types referenced below (`InsertOutcome`, `TombstoneRow`, `WatermarkKey`, `ClaimerId`, `StoreError`, etc.) are defined in [`trait/types.md`](trait/types.md) and live in `crates/nmp-core/src/store/types.rs`.

## 2. The trait

```rust
pub trait EventStore: Send + Sync {
    // ─────── Reads ───────

    /// Primary lookup. Returns Ok(None) if absent; tombstones do not count as "present".
    fn get_by_id(&self, id: &EventId) -> Result<Option<StoredEvent>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_author_kind` scan, newest-first.
    /// `kinds` must be non-empty; callers wanting any-kind use `scan_by_kind_time` instead.
    fn scan_by_author_kind<'a>(
        &'a self,
        author: &PubKey,
        kinds: &[u32],
        since: Option<u64>,
        until: Option<u64>,
        limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_kind_dtag` lookup. Returns the current authoritative parameterized
    /// replaceable for `(pubkey, kind, d_tag)`, or Ok(None).
    fn get_param_replaceable(
        &self,
        pubkey: &PubKey,
        kind: u32,
        d_tag: &[u8],
    ) -> Result<Option<StoredEvent>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_kind_dtag_time` scan, newest-first across all authors for `(kind, d_tag)`.
    /// Used for global parameterized-replaceable discovery (e.g. "recent articles with slug X").
    /// To list all replaceables by a specific author use `scan_by_author_kind` instead.
    fn scan_by_kind_dtag<'a>(
        &'a self,
        kind: u32,
        d_tag: &[u8],
        since: Option<u64>,
        until: Option<u64>,
        limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_etag_time` scan, newest-first. Used by reaction / repost / thread views.
    /// `kinds` must be non-empty; pass `&[7]` for reactions, `&[6]` for reposts, etc.
    fn scan_by_etag<'a>(
        &'a self,
        target: &EventId,
        kinds: &[u32],
        limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_ptag_time` scan, newest-first. Used by notifications / mention views.
    /// `kinds` must be non-empty.
    fn scan_by_ptag<'a>(
        &'a self,
        target: &PubKey,
        kinds: &[u32],
        limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_kind_time` scan, newest-first. Pass `kinds = &[]` to scan all kinds
    /// (the only scan method that accepts an empty kinds slice).
    fn scan_by_kind_time<'a>(
        &'a self,
        kinds: &[u32],
        since: Option<u64>,
        until: Option<u64>,
        limit: usize,
    ) -> Result<Box<dyn EventIter + 'a>, StoreError>;

    /// `idx_expires` scan, ascending — used by the NIP-40 reaper.
    fn scan_expiring_before<'a>(
        &'a self,
        unix_seconds: u64,
        limit: usize,
    /// Soft hint: keep these in hot LRU on a best-effort basis.
    fn hot_set_hint(&self, ids: &[EventId]) -> Result<(), StoreError>;

    /// One bounded GC pass — reap expired, trim LRU, purge old tombstones.
    fn gc_step(&self, budget: GcBudget) -> Result<GcReport, StoreError>;

    // ─────── Domain rows (per-DomainModule typed namespace) ───────

    fn domain_open(&self, namespace: &'static str) -> Result<DomainHandle<'_>, StoreError>;
    fn run_migrations(&self, namespace: &'static str, target_version: u32,
                      migrations: &[crate::substrate::DomainMigration])
        -> Result<(), StoreError>;

    // ─────── Export ───────

    fn dump(&self, out: &mut dyn std::io::Write, format: DumpFormat)
        -> Result<DumpStats, StoreError>;
}
```

`DeleteFilter` mirrors the limited subset of admin operations the kernel needs (by-relay-only events, by-author, by-id-list, by-kind range); it is **not** a pass-through to `nostr::Filter` — we intentionally do not expose arbitrary remote filters as a delete vector.

`Coverage` (returned by `coverage()`):

```rust
pub enum Coverage {
    CompleteAsOf(u64),  // fully synced; a cache miss is authoritative "doesn't exist"
    PartialUpTo(u64),   // synced up to timestamp but row is stale — fetch is needed
    Unknown,            // no watermark; always fetch
}
```

 //! | Outcome | Meaning |
 //! |---|---|
 //! | `Send(bytes)` | Forward `bytes` to the peer, then call `step` again with the response. |
-//! | `Done { synced, have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`crate::SyncStrategy::resume_state`] persistence. |
+//! | `Done { have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`nmp_core::store::WatermarkRow::last_negentropy_state`] persistence. |
 //!
 //! ## Roles
 //!
 //! Negentropy is asymmetric — the *client* drives the protocol, the *server*
 //! responds to fingerprint queries.  The reconciler factory mirrors this:
 //!
-//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client (`set_initiator` is
-//!   true by construction; first call to [`Reconciler::step`] with `None`
-//!   produces the initial query).
+//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client; first call to
+//!   [`Reconciler::step`] with `None` produces the initial query.
 //! * [`Reconciler::server`] builds a responding server.  Calling
 //!   [`Reconciler::step`] without a peer payload on a server is a programmer
 //!   error and returns [`ReconcilerError::ServerNotInitiator`].

 //! | Outcome | Meaning |
 //! |---|---|
 //! | `Send(bytes)` | Forward `bytes` to the peer, then call `step` again with the response. |
-//! | `Done { synced, have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`crate::SyncStrategy::resume_state`] persistence. |
+//! | `Done { have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`nmp_core::store::WatermarkRow::last_negentropy_state`] persistence. |
 //!
 //! ## Roles
 //!
 //! Negentropy is asymmetric — the *client* drives the protocol, the *server*
 //! responds to fingerprint queries.  The reconciler factory mirrors this:
 //!
-//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client (`set_initiator` is
-//!   true by construction; first call to [`Reconciler::step`] with `None`
-//!   produces the initial query).
+//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client; first call to
+//!   [`Reconciler::step`] with `None` produces the initial query.
 //! * [`Reconciler::server`] builds a responding server.  Calling
 //!   [`Reconciler::step`] without a peer payload on a server is a programmer
 //!   error and returns [`ReconcilerError::ServerNotInitiator`].

diff --git a/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs b/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs
index fe427d64daf267817dbf05f68d2dc51b08d03a85..1e777487c031a696e55d68739997bb8dc0b0fbee
--- a/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs
+++ b/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs
@@ -8,16 +8,15 @@
 //! | Outcome | Meaning |
 //! |---|---|
 //! | `Send(bytes)` | Forward `bytes` to the peer, then call `step` again with the response. |
-//! | `Done { synced, have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`crate::SyncStrategy::resume_state`] persistence. |
+//! | `Done { have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`nmp_core::store::WatermarkRow::last_negentropy_state`] persistence. |
 //!
 //! ## Roles
 //!
 //! Negentropy is asymmetric — the *client* drives the protocol, the *server*
 //! responds to fingerprint queries.  The reconciler factory mirrors this:
 //!
-//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client (`set_initiator` is
-//!   true by construction; first call to [`Reconciler::step`] with `None`
-//!   produces the initial query).
+//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client; first call to
+//!   [`Reconciler::step`] with `None` produces the initial query.
 //! * [`Reconciler::server`] builds a responding server.  Calling
 //!   [`Reconciler::step`] without a peer payload on a server is a programmer
 //!   error and returns [`ReconcilerError::ServerNotInitiator`].

 //! | Outcome | Meaning |
 //! |---|---|
 //! | `Send(bytes)` | Forward `bytes` to the peer, then call `step` again with the response. |
-//! | `Done { synced, have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`crate::SyncStrategy::resume_state`] persistence. |
+//! | `Done { have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`nmp_core::store::WatermarkRow::last_negentropy_state`] persistence. |
 //!
 //! ## Roles
 //!
 //! Negentropy is asymmetric — the *client* drives the protocol, the *server*
 //! responds to fingerprint queries.  The reconciler factory mirrors this:
 //!
-//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client (`set_initiator` is
-//!   true by construction; first call to [`Reconciler::step`] with `None`
-//!   produces the initial query).
+//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client; first call to
+//!   [`Reconciler::step`] with `None` produces the initial query.
 //! * [`Reconciler::server`] builds a responding server.  Calling
 //!   [`Reconciler::step`] without a peer payload on a server is a programmer
 //!   error and returns [`ReconcilerError::ServerNotInitiator`].

--- a/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs
+++ b/crates/nmp-nip77/src/reconciler.rs
@@ -8,16 +8,15 @@
 //! | Outcome | Meaning |
 //! |---|---|
 //! | `Send(bytes)` | Forward `bytes` to the peer, then call `step` again with the response. |
-//! | `Done { synced, have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`crate::SyncStrategy::resume_state`] persistence. |
+//! | `Done { have, need, state }` | Reconciliation converged.  `have` are ids the peer must accept from us; `need` are ids we should pull. `state` is an opaque resume blob suitable for [`nmp_core::store::WatermarkRow::last_negentropy_state`] persistence. |
 //!
 //! ## Roles
 //!
 //! Negentropy is asymmetric — the *client* drives the protocol, the *server*
 //! responds to fingerprint queries.  The reconciler factory mirrors this:
 //!
-//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client (`set_initiator` is
-//!   true by construction; first call to [`Reconciler::step`] with `None`
-//!   produces the initial query).
+//! * [`Reconciler::client`] builds an initiating client; first call to
+//!   [`Reconciler::step`] with `None` produces the initial query.
 //! * [`Reconciler::server`] builds a responding server.  Calling
 //!   [`Reconciler::step`] without a peer payload on a server is a programmer
 //!   error and returns [`ReconcilerError::ServerNotInitiator`].

     8	//! | Strategy | Plan rewrite |
     9	//! |---|---|
    10	//! | `SkipReq` | Sub-shape dropped from the relay plan; relay's plan removed if empty. |
    11	//! | `ReqSince(s)` | Sub-shape's `since` is bumped to `s` (no-op if existing `since` is already ≥ `s`). |
    12	//! | `NegThenReq` | Sub-shape preserved; the planner emits the REQ unchanged.  The companion negentropy run happens on the parallel sync path. |
    13	//! | `Resume { next, .. }` | Same as `next`; the resume blob is consumed by the negentropy run, not the planner. |
    63	/// Rewrite `plan` in place per the M4 coverage gate.
    64	///
    65	/// `canonicalise` maps a sub-shape's filter to the 32-byte canonical filter
    66	/// hash expected by [`WatermarkKey::filter_hash`].  The kernel will eventually
    67	/// expose `canonical_filter_hash(&Filter)` (see `docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md`
    68	/// §3); until it does, callers pass their own hash function — keeping
    69	/// `nmp-nip77` decoupled from the (still-design-stage) canonical encoder.
    70	pub fn apply_coverage_filter<F>(
    82	    for (relay_url, relay_plan) in plan.per_relay.iter_mut() {
    83	        relay_plan.sub_shapes.retain_mut(|sub| {
    84	            let filter_hash = canonicalise(sub);
    85	            let key = WatermarkKey {
    86	                filter_hash,
    87	                relay_url: relay_url.clone(),
    88	            };
    89	            let coverage = store.coverage(&key).unwrap_or(nmp_core::store::Coverage::Unknown);
    90	            let watermark = store.read_watermark(&key).ok().flatten();
    91	            let capabilities = caps.get(relay_url);
    92	            let strategy = decide_strategy(
    93	                &key,
    94	                GateInputs {
    95	                    coverage,
    96	                    capabilities,
    97	                    watermark,
    98	                },
    99	            );
   100	            let (keep, decision) = apply_strategy_to_sub(sub, &strategy);
   101	            report.decisions.insert(
   102	                (relay_url.clone(), hex32(&filter_hash)),
   103	                decision,
   104	            );
   105	            keep
   117	fn apply_strategy_to_sub(
   118	    sub: &mut nmp_core::planner::SubShape,
   119	    strategy: &SyncStrategy,
   120	) -> (bool, GateDecision) {
   121	    match strategy.inner() {
   122	        SyncStrategy::SkipReq => (false, GateDecision::Skipped),
   123	        SyncStrategy::ReqSince(since) => {
   124	            if sub.shape.since.map(|s| s < *since).unwrap_or(true) {
   125	                sub.shape.since = Some(*since);
   126	                (true, GateDecision::BumpedSince(*since))
   127	            } else {
   128	                (true, GateDecision::Kept)
   129	            }
   130	        }
   131	        SyncStrategy::NegThenReq => (true, GateDecision::Kept),
   132	        // `Resume` is collapsed by `.inner()`, so it's unreachable here.

    41	    }

    46	/// C1: Replaceable-event supersession (kind 0 / 3 / 10000-19999) on insert.
    47	/// Design: `docs/design/framework-magic/replaceable.md` §C1.
    48	#[test]
    49	fn c1_replaceable_supersedes_on_insert() {
    50	    let h = StoreHarness::mem();
    51	
    52	    let ev1 = h.make_event(ALICE_HEX, 0, 1_000);
    53	    let id1 = ev1.id_bytes();
    54	    assert!(matches!(h.insert_raw(ev1, "wss://r1/", 1_000_000), InsertOutcome::Inserted { .. }));
    55	    h.assert_present(&id1);
    56	
    57	    let ev2 = h.make_event(ALICE_HEX, 0, 2_000);
    58	    let id2 = ev2.id_bytes();
    59	    let o2 = h.insert_raw(ev2, "wss://r1/", 2_000_000);
    60	    assert!(matches!(o2, InsertOutcome::Replaced { .. }), "newer must replace: {o2:?}");
    61	    h.assert_absent(&id1);
    62	    h.assert_present(&id2);
    63	
    64	    let ev_stale = h.make_event(ALICE_HEX, 0, 500);
    65	    let id_stale = ev_stale.id_bytes();
    66	    let o_stale = h.insert_raw(ev_stale, "wss://r2/", 3_000_000);
    67	    assert!(matches!(o_stale, InsertOutcome::Superseded { .. }), "stale: {o_stale:?}");
    68	    h.assert_absent(&id_stale);
    69	    h.assert_present(&id2);
    70	
    71	    // Tie-break at same created_at: lexicographically smaller id wins.
    72	    // Use BOB_HEX so we don't conflict with Alice's kind:0 slot.
    73	    let id_large = "f".repeat(64);
    74	    let id_small = "0".repeat(64);
    75	    let ev_large = h.make_event_with_id(&id_large, BOB_HEX, 0, 5_000);
    76	    let large_id_bytes = ev_large.id_bytes();
    77	    h.insert_raw(ev_large, "wss://r1/", 5_000_000);
    78	    h.assert_present(&large_id_bytes);
    79	
    80	    let ev_small = h.make_event_with_id(&id_small, BOB_HEX, 0, 5_000);

    12	//! ## Threshold
    13	//!
    14	//! The task description fixes the cutover at **95 %** coverage and *recent*
    15	//! freshness.  Freshness comes from the store's `Coverage::CompleteAsOf`
    16	//! signal, which already encodes the 300-second staleness window from
    17	//! `docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md` §1.1.  We never re-implement that check
    18	//! here.
    19	//!
    20	//! ## D6
    21	//!
    22	//! [`decide_strategy`] is infallible — every input maps to a strategy.  No
    23	//! error type, no `Result`.  The planner never has a reason to surface a
    24	//! "coverage decision failed" toast.
    25	
    26	use nmp_core::store::{Coverage, WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow};
    27	
    28	use crate::capability::RelayCapabilities;
    29	
    30	/// Coverage proportion threshold above which a `CompleteAsOf` row earns
    31	/// `SyncStrategy::SkipReq`.  Documented at 95 % in the M4 task spec; kept
    32	/// public so callers and tests don't hard-code the constant in their own
    33	/// asserts.
    34	pub const COVERAGE_THRESHOLD_PCT: u8 = 95;
   121	/// Compute the simple coverage percentage helper documented in the task
   122	/// description (`coverage > 95% and recent` → `SkipReq`).  The store's
   123	/// `Coverage` enum already collapses staleness into the `CompleteAsOf` vs
   124	/// `PartialUpTo` distinction, so the percentage path is informational only —
   125	/// useful for diagnostics + tests that want to assert "we cleared 95 %".
   126	pub fn coverage_pct(coverage: Coverage, now_s: u64) -> u8 {
   127	    match coverage {
   128	        Coverage::CompleteAsOf(_) => 100,
   129	        Coverage::Unknown => 0,
   130	        Coverage::PartialUpTo(ts) => {
   131	            if now_s == 0 || ts == 0 {
   132	                return 0;
   133	            }
   134	            let ratio = (ts as f64 / now_s as f64).clamp(0.0, 1.0);
   135	            (ratio * 100.0).round() as u8
   136	        }
   137	    }
   138	}
   141	    /// item set.  At the moment the `negentropy` 0.5 crate does not expose a
   142	    /// public deserializer, so we re-seed a client with the current items
   143	    /// (correctness preserved — the protocol converges deterministically) and
   144	    /// surface the `state` blob only as a *coverage hint*.  Persisting the
   145	    /// blob is still useful so future engine versions can resume mid-frame.
   146	    pub fn resume_client(
   147	        items: Vec<SyncedItem>,
   148	        _state: &[u8],
   149	    ) -> Result<Self, ReconcilerError> {
   150	        Self::client(items)
   151	    }
   152	
    60	## Limitations
    61	
    62	- The reconciler is exercised in-process; a real-relay measurement
    63	  (against `strfry` / `relay-builder`) is deferred.  The protocol contract
    64	  is identical, so the bytes-on-wire numbers will match within a small
    65	  protocol-version-byte rounding margin.
    66	- `Reconciler::resume_client` accepts a state blob but the `negentropy`
    67	  0.5 crate does not expose a public deserializer, so the blob currently
    68	  acts as a coverage hint, not a true mid-stream resume.  Persisting it is
    69	  still useful so future engine versions can pick up mid-frame.
    70	- Capability persistence is wired through [`CapabilityDomain`](../../../crates/nmp-nip77/src/capability_domain.rs)
    71	  as a `DomainModule`, but the LMDB-backed store path is not yet active
    72	  in M4 (M3 + LMDB feature gate); the in-memory cache covers the run-time
    73	  semantics.
    74	
    75	## Follow-ups
    76	
    77	- Live measurement against a real NIP-77 relay (defer to M11 hardware
    78	  proof window or M11.5 highlighter slice).
    79	- Wire `apply_coverage_filter` into the M2 planner's hot path (currently
    80	  exposed at the crate-public API but not yet called from the actor; the
    81	  actor remains M1-era code).
    82	- Add `canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` to `nmp-core::store`
    83	  per `docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md` §3, so the planner gate doesn't
    84	  need to take a custom canonicalisation closure.

     1	# M4 — NIP-77 negentropy sync engine
     2	
     3	> Part of the [Build & Validation Plan](../plan.md). Arc 1 — Kernel substrate + Nostr social stack.
     4	
     5	**Demo product:** Profile screen for a new author cold-syncs via NIP-77 against primal, visibly faster and with measured bytes savings vs REQ scan.
     6	
     7	**Scope.** Per `product-spec.md` §7.8 and ADR (sync as engine, not feature):
     8	
     9	**Subsystem deliverables.**
    10	
    11	- `nmp-nip77` protocol module: negentropy reconciliation client (use `nostr-sdk`'s implementation or `negentropy` crate directly).
    12	- Sync watermarks table active per-`(filter, relay)`.
    13	- Planner consults watermarks before issuing historical REQ; sync-first backfill with REQ as fallback (when relay doesn't support NIP-77).
    14	- Three built-in triggers: app foreground, view-open-with-gap, relay reconnect.
    15	- `RunSync` manual action module.
    16	- Per-relay NIP-77 capability negotiation (probe + cache result).
    17	- Bytes-saved counter in diagnostics.
    18	
    19	**Exit gate.**
    20	
    21	- Cold open of a profile against primal: completes via negentropy, not REQ. Bytes-on-wire ≤ 5% of equivalent REQ on a 10k-event backfill.
    22	- Cache-miss against a fully-synced `(filter, relay)` pair answers authoritatively (no fallback fetch).
    23	- Relay reconnect after 10 min resumes from watermark; gap filled by sync.
    24	- Mixed-capability test (one NIP-77 relay, one non-NIP-77): both populate the same store; non-NIP-77 falls back to REQ; bytes-saved diagnostic reflects the split.
    25	
    26	**Runnable artifact.** iOS app with measurably faster profile cold-opens. Report in `docs/perf/m4/negentropy.md`.

    74	impl ClientFrame {
    75	    /// Render this frame as a JSON string suitable for a WebSocket text
    76	    /// payload.
    77	    pub fn to_text(&self) -> String {
    78	        let value: Value = match self {
    79	            ClientFrame::Open {
    80	                sub_id,
    81	                filter,
    82	                initial_msg,
    83	            } => json!(["NEG-OPEN", sub_id, filter, hex_encode(initial_msg)]),
    84	            ClientFrame::Msg { sub_id, msg } => json!(["NEG-MSG", sub_id, hex_encode(msg)]),
    85	            ClientFrame::Close { sub_id } => json!(["NEG-CLOSE", sub_id]),
    86	        };
    87	        value.to_string()
    88	    }
   136	
   137	fn hex_encode(bytes: &[u8]) -> String {
   138	    static HEX: &[u8; 16] = b"0123456789abcdef";
   139	    let mut out = String::with_capacity(bytes.len() * 2);
   140	    for b in bytes {
   141	        out.push(HEX[(b >> 4) as usize] as char);
   142	        out.push(HEX[(b & 0x0F) as usize] as char);
   143	    }
   144	    out
   145	}
   146	
   147	fn hex_decode(s: &str) -> Result<Vec<u8>, WireError> {
   148	    if !s.len().is_multiple_of(2) {
   149	        return Err(WireError::InvalidHex);
   150	    }
   151	    let mut out = Vec::with_capacity(s.len() / 2);
   152	    let bytes = s.as_bytes();
   153	    for chunk in bytes.chunks(2) {
   154	        let hi = hex_nibble(chunk[0])?;
   155	        let lo = hex_nibble(chunk[1])?;
   156	        out.push((hi << 4) | lo);
   157	    }
   158	    Ok(out)
   159	}
   160	
   161	fn hex_nibble(b: u8) -> Result<u8, WireError> {
   162	    match b {
   163	        b'0'..=b'9' => Ok(b - b'0'),
   164	        b'a'..=b'f' => Ok(b - b'a' + 10),
    54	
    55	/// Thread-safe in-memory counters.
    56	pub struct SyncMetrics {
    57	    inner: Mutex<HashMap<RelayFilterKey, PairCounters>>,
    58	}
    59	
    60	impl SyncMetrics {
    61	    pub fn new() -> Self {
    62	        Self {
    63	            inner: Mutex::new(HashMap::new()),
    64	        }
    65	    }
    66	
    67	    /// Add `n` bytes to the negentropy-on-wire counter for this pair.
    68	    pub fn record_neg_bytes(&self, key: &RelayFilterKey, n: u64) {
    69	        let mut guard = self.inner.lock().expect("metrics lock poisoned");
    70	        let entry = guard.entry(key.clone()).or_default();
    71	        entry.bytes_on_wire_via_neg = entry.bytes_on_wire_via_neg.saturating_add(n);
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    /// Record a (REQ-baseline, neg-actual) pair, attributing the saving (or
    75	    /// the regression — clamped to 0) to this pair.
    76	    pub fn record_savings(&self, key: &RelayFilterKey, req_baseline: u64, neg_actual: u64) {
    77	        let saving = req_baseline.saturating_sub(neg_actual);
    78	        let mut guard = self.inner.lock().expect("metrics lock poisoned");
    79	        let entry = guard.entry(key.clone()).or_default();
    80	        entry.bytes_saved_vs_req = entry.bytes_saved_vs_req.saturating_add(saving);
    81	    }
    82	
    83	    pub fn snapshot(&self) -> MetricsSnapshot {
    84	        let guard = self.inner.lock().expect("metrics lock poisoned");
    85	        let per_pair = guard.clone();
    86	        let mut totals = TotalCounters::default();
    87	        for c in per_pair.values() {
    88	            totals.bytes_on_wire_via_neg = totals
    89	                .bytes_on_wire_via_neg
    90	                .saturating_add(c.bytes_on_wire_via_neg);
    91	            totals.bytes_saved_vs_req = totals

**Orchestrator Follow-Up**

- D2 violation: [planner_gate.rs](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/.claude/worktrees/agent-ade0f26d140a43ad2/crates/nmp-nip77/src/planner_gate.rs:12) and [planner_gate.rs](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/.claude/worktrees/agent-ade0f26d140a43ad2/crates/nmp-nip77/src/planner_gate.rs:131) keep `NegThenReq` as an unchanged REQ. Historical backfill must run negentropy first, then emit an ids-scoped REQ only for `need`. Keep live tail REQ separate.
